## <span style="color:#FFC107">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-20 12:40:56]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FFC107; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">



6 audit agents are running in the background. I'll report results as they come in.  

Regarding your authentication question — you're raising an important point. Here's what I can say before the auth audit agent reports back:  

**The current situation (Phase 1):**  
- The app binds to `localhost:23000` only — the security model relies on OS-level isolation (only local processes can connect)  
- `X-Agent-Id` is a self-declared header with **no cryptographic verification** at the API layer  
- AMP messaging does have Ed25519 signing for message authenticity, but that's for inter-agent messages, not for governance API calls  

**The gap you're identifying:**  
- Any local process that can reach `localhost:23000` can set `X-Agent-Id` to any value  
- This means an agent could impersonate another agent to bypass governance restrictions (e.g., pretend to be the MANAGER to delete a closed team)  
- For localhost-only Phase 1, this is partially mitigated by the assumption that all agents are trusted local processes  
- But if the governance rules are meant to enforce real organizational policies, this trust model is insufficient  

**What would be needed:**  
- Agent authentication via API keys or signed requests (similar to how AMP already signs messages with Ed25519)  
- Each agent registers with a key pair; API calls must include a signature or bearer token  
- The `X-Agent-Id` would then be verified against the authenticated identity, not just trusted  

The auth audit agent is investigating the exact current state. Once all 6 agents report, I'll consolidate the findings and we can discuss whether to create a GitHub issue for agent API authentication.  

</div>

    14→- **Confidence:** CONFIRMED  
    15→- **Description:** The GET, PUT, and DELETE handlers in `[docId]/route.ts` never extract `X-Agent-Id` from the request headers and never pass `requestingAgentId` to the service functions. This means all three operations on individual documents completely bypass the governance ACL for closed teams. Any agent (or any local process) can read, modify, or delete documents in a closed team.  
    16→- **Evidence:**  
    17→  - GET (line 6): `_request: NextRequest` -- request is unused, `getTeamDocument(id, docId)` called with only 2 args

    19→  - DELETE (line 39): `_request: NextRequest` -- request is unused, `deleteTeamDocument(id, docId)` called with only 2 args  
    20→- **Fix:** Extract `requestingAgentId` from request headers in all three handlers (matching the pattern used in every other route file). Pass it to the service function calls. For PUT, spread it into the params object. For GET and DELETE, pass as the 3rd argument.  
    21→

   121→export function listAllTeams(): ServiceResult<{ teams: any[] }> {  
   122→  const teams = loadTeams()  
   123→  return { data: { teams }, status: 200 }  
   124→}  
   125→  
   126→/**  
   127→ * Create a new team.  
   128→ * Governance: validates team type, passes managerId and agentNames to createTeam  
   129→ * for business rule enforcement (R1-R4).  
   130→ */  
   131→export async function createNewTeam(params: CreateTeamParams): Promise<ServiceResult<{ team: any }>> {  
   132→  const { name, description, agentIds } = params  
   133→  
   134→  if (!name || typeof name !== 'string') {  
   135→    return { error: 'Team name is required', status: 400 }  
   136→  }  
   137→  
   138→  if (agentIds && !Array.isArray(agentIds)) {  
   139→    return { error: 'agentIds must be an array', status: 400 }  
   140→  }  
   141→  
   142→  // Governance: validate type field  
   143→  if (params.type && params.type !== 'open' && params.type !== 'closed') {  
   144→    return { error: 'type must be "open" or "closed"', status: 400 }  
   145→  }  
   146→  
   147→  try {  
   148→    // Pass governance context (managerId + agent names for collision checks) to createTeam  
   149→    const managerId = getManagerId()  
   150→    const agentNames = loadAgents().map(a => a.name).filter(Boolean)  
   151→    const team = await createTeam(  
   152→      { name, description, agentIds: agentIds || [], type: params.type, chiefOfStaffId: params.chiefOfStaffId },  
   153→      managerId,  
   154→      agentNames  
   155→    )  
   156→    return { data: { team }, status: 201 }  
   157→  } catch (error) {  
   158→    // TeamValidationException carries a specific HTTP status code from governance rules  
   159→    if (error instanceof TeamValidationException) {  
   160→      return { error: error.message, status: error.code }  
   161→    }  
   162→    console.error('Failed to create team:', error)  
   163→    return { error: error instanceof Error ? error.message : 'Failed to create team', status: 500 }  
   164→  }  
   165→}

    36→export function sanitizeTeamName(raw: string): string {  
    37→  return raw  
    38→    .replace(/[\x00-\x1F\x7F]/g, '')  // Strip control characters (same as agent name sanitization)  
    39→    .replace(/\s+/g, ' ')              // Collapse all whitespace into single space

    42→  
    43→/**  
    44→ * Validate a team mutation (create or update) against all governance business rules.  
    45→ *  
    46→ * Rules enforced:  
    47→ * - R1.3/R1.4: Closed team must have a COS (COS-closed invariant)  
    48→ * - R1.7: TeamType must be 'open' or 'closed'  
    49→ * - R1.8: COS can only be set on a closed team  
    50→ * - R2.1/R2.3: Team names must be unique (case-insensitive)  
    51→ * - R4.1: Normal agents can be in at most one closed team  
    52→ * - R4.6: COS must be a member of the team (auto-added to agentIds)  
    53→ * - R4.7: Cannot remove COS from agentIds while they are chiefOfStaffId  
    54→ * - Team name sanitization: min 4 chars, max 64 chars, alphanumeric start, safe characters only  
    55→ *  
    56→ * @param teams - Current teams list (for uniqueness and multi-closed checks)  
    57→ * @param teamId - null for create, team ID for update  
    58→ * @param data - Proposed team data or updates  
    59→ * @param managerId - Current MANAGER agent ID (for multi-closed-team exemption check)  
    60→ * @param reservedNames - Optional list of names that cannot be used (e.g., agent names) — prevents team/agent name collisions  
    61→ * @returns Object with valid:true and sanitized corrections, or valid:false with error details  
    62→ */

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-20 12:41:07]*

<summary>🔧 Tool: Read -- `message-filter.ts`</summary>

**Input:**

  "file_path": "/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/message-filter.ts",
  "offset": 1,
  "limit": 180

**Result:**

     1→/**  
     2→ * Message Filter — enforces closed-team messaging isolation  
     3→ *  
     4→ * Determines whether a message from sender to recipient is allowed  
     5→ * based on governance roles (MANAGER, Chief-of-Staff) and closed-team  
     6→ * membership. Open-world agents (not in any closed team) can message  
     7→ * freely unless the recipient is inside a closed team.  
     8→ */  
     9→  
    10→import { loadGovernance } from './governance'  
    11→import { loadTeams } from './team-registry'  
    12→import { isValidUuid } from './validation'  
    13→  
    14→export interface MessageFilterInput {  
    15→  senderAgentId: string | null // null = mesh-forwarded message  
    16→  recipientAgentId: string  
    17→}  
    18→  
    19→export interface MessageFilterResult {  
    20→  allowed: boolean  
    21→  reason?: string  
    22→}  
    23→  
    24→/**  
    25→ * Check whether a message from sender to recipient is allowed.  
    26→ *  
    27→ * Algorithm (R6.1–R6.7):  
    28→ * 1. Mesh-forwarded (senderAgentId null): denied if recipient is in a closed team (unverified sender)  
    29→ * 1b. Unresolved recipient (alias, not UUID) from closed-team sender: denied (prevents bypass)  
    30→ * 2. Neither in a closed team: allowed (open world, current behavior) (R6.4)  
    31→ * 3. Sender is MANAGER: always allowed (R6.3)

    31→export function loadDocuments(teamId: string): TeamDocument[] {  
    32→  try {  
    33→    ensureTeamsDir()  
    34→    const filePath = docsFilePath(teamId)  
    35→    if (!fs.existsSync(filePath)) {  
    36→      return []  
    37→    }  
    38→    const data = fs.readFileSync(filePath, 'utf-8')  
    39→    const parsed: TeamDocumentsFile = JSON.parse(data)  
    40→    return Array.isArray(parsed.documents) ? parsed.documents : []  
    41→  } catch (error) {  
    42→    console.error(`Failed to load documents for team ${teamId}:`, error)  
    43→    return []  
    44→  }  
    45→}  
    46→  
    47→export function saveDocuments(teamId: string, documents: TeamDocument[]): boolean {  
    48→  try {  
    49→    ensureTeamsDir()  
    50→    const file: TeamDocumentsFile = { version: 1, documents }  
    51→    fs.writeFileSync(docsFilePath(teamId), JSON.stringify(file, null, 2), 'utf-8')  
    52→    return true  
    53→  } catch (error) {  
    54→    console.error(`Failed to save documents for team ${teamId}:`, error)  
    55→    return false  
    56→  }  
    57→}  
    58→

    88→export async function notifyAgent(options: NotificationOptions): Promise<NotificationResult> {  
    89→  // Check if notifications are enabled  
    90→  if (!NOTIFICATIONS_ENABLED) {  
    91→    return { success: true, notified: false, reason: 'Notifications disabled' }

   104→    // Use isSelf() for robust hostname comparison (handles variations like 'mac-mini' vs 'mac-mini.local')  
   105→    if (agentHost && agentHost !== 'local' && !isSelf(agentHost)) {  
   106→      // Target is genuinely on a remote host - skip notification  
   107→      // (Remote host will handle its own notification when it receives the message)  
   108→      console.log(`[Notify] Agent ${agentName} is on remote host ${agentHost} (self: ${selfHostId}), skipping notification`)  
   109→      return { success: true, notified: false, reason: `Remote host: ${agentHost}` }  
   110→    }  
   111→  
   112→    // Look up the agent  
   113→    let agent = agentId ? getAgent(agentId) : null  
   114→    if (!agent) {  
   115→      agent = getAgentByName(agentName, selfHostId)  
   116→    }  
   117→  
   118→    if (!agent) {  
   119→      console.log(`[Notify] Agent ${agentName} not found in registry`)  
   120→      return { success: true, notified: false, reason: 'Agent not found' }  
   121→    }

    11→- **File:** /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/tests/transfer-registry.test.ts:50-51  
    12→- **Severity:** MUST-FIX  
    13→- **Category:** logic  
    14→- **Confidence:** CONFIRMED  
    15→- **Description:** The test helper computes `TRANSFERS_FILE` using `os.homedir()` (line 51), but the source `lib/transfer-registry.ts` computes it using `process.env.HOME || '~'` (line 15). On most systems these are identical, but if `process.env.HOME` is unset or differs from `os.homedir()`, the `seedTransfers()` helper writes to a path that the module never reads, causing tests to silently pass with empty data rather than seeded data. This is a real portability bug.  
    16→- **Evidence:**  
    17→  ```typescript  
    18→  // test (line 50-51):  
    19→  const AI_MAESTRO_DIR = path.join(os.homedir(), '.aimaestro')  
    20→  const TRANSFERS_FILE = path.join(AI_MAESTRO_DIR, 'governance-transfers.json')  
    21→  
    22→  // source (lib/transfer-registry.ts line 15-16):  
    23→  const AI_MAESTRO_DIR = path.join(process.env.HOME || '~', '.aimaestro')  
    24→  const TRANSFERS_FILE = path.join(AI_MAESTRO_DIR, 'governance-transfers.json')  
    25→  ```  
    26→- **Fix:** Change the test to use `process.env.HOME || '~'` to match the source, or better yet, mock `process.env.HOME` explicitly in `beforeEach` to guarantee consistency.

    26→  
    27→  let body  
    28→  try {  
    29→    body = await request.json()  
    30→  } catch {  
    31→    return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Invalid JSON body' }, { status: 400 })  
    32→  }  
    33→  
    34→  const result = await createTeamDocument(id, { ...body, requestingAgentId })  
    35→  
    36→  if (result.error) {  
    37→    return NextResponse.json({ error: result.error }, { status: result.status })  
    38→  }  
    39→  return NextResponse.json(result.data, { status: result.status })  
    40→}  
    41→

   594→/**  
   595→ * Notify team agents about a meeting.  
   596→ */  
   597→export async function notifyTeamAgents(params: NotifyTeamParams): Promise<ServiceResult<{ results: any[] }>> {  
   598→  const { agentIds, teamName } = params  
   599→  
   600→  if (!agentIds || !Array.isArray(agentIds)) {  
   601→    return { error: 'agentIds array is required', status: 400 }  
   602→  }  
   603→  
   604→  if (!teamName || typeof teamName !== 'string') {  
   605→    return { error: 'teamName is required', status: 400 }  
   606→  }  
   607→  
   608→  try {  
   609→    const results = await Promise.all(  
   610→      agentIds.map(async (agentId: string) => {  
   611→        const agent = getAgent(agentId)  
   612→        if (!agent) {  
   613→          return { agentId, success: false, reason: 'Agent not found' }  
   614→        }  
   615→  
   616→        const agentName = agent.name || agent.alias || 'unknown'  
   617→        try {  
   618→          const result = await notifyAgent({  
   619→            agentId: agent.id,  
   620→            agentName,  
   621→            agentHost: agent.hostId,  
   622→            fromName: 'AI Maestro',  
   623→            subject: `Team "${teamName}" is starting`,  
   624→            messageId: `meeting-${Date.now()}`,  
   625→            messageType: 'notification',  
   626→          })  
   627→          return { agentId, agentName, ...result }  
   628→        } catch (error) {  
   629→          return { agentId, agentName, success: false, error: String(error) }  
   630→        }  
   631→      })  
   632→    )  
   633→  
   634→    return { data: { results }, status: 200 }  
   635→  } catch (error) {  
   636→    console.error('Failed to notify team:', error)  
   637→    return { error: error instanceof Error ? error.message : 'Failed to notify team', status: 500 }  
   638→  }  
   639→}

    26→ * Decision order:

    33→ *  7. Otherwise                → denied

    39→  // where all local processes are trusted.

    41→  // genuine web UI requests from other local processes.  
    42→  if (input.requestingAgentId === undefined) {

    80→  
    81→// Phase 1: No lock on read. Minor TOCTOU with setPassword(). Acceptable for single-user localhost.  
    82→// Returns false for both 'no password set' and 'wrong password'.  
    83→// Callers should check hasPassword (config.passwordHash) separately if they need to distinguish.  
    84→/** Verify plaintext against stored password hash. Returns false if no password set. */  
    85→export async function verifyPassword(plaintext: string): Promise<boolean> {  
    86→  const config = loadGovernance()  
    87→  if (!config.passwordHash) {  
    88→    // Phase 1 (localhost-only): timing difference between "no password" and "wrong password"  
    89→    // is accepted risk. No remote attackers can observe timing in this deployment model.  
    90→    return false  
    91→  }  
    92→  return bcrypt.compare(plaintext, config.passwordHash)  
    93→}

   204→  
   205→export function loadTeams(): Team[] {  
   206→  try {  
   207→    ensureTeamsDir()  
   208→    if (!fs.existsSync(TEAMS_FILE)) {  
   209→      return []  
   210→    }  
   211→    const data = fs.readFileSync(TEAMS_FILE, 'utf-8')  
   212→    const parsed: TeamsFile = JSON.parse(data)  
   213→    const teams = Array.isArray(parsed.teams) ? parsed.teams : []  
   214→  
   215→    // Idempotent convergent migration: ensure all teams have a type field (default to 'open').  
   216→    // If two concurrent calls both trigger the migration, both produce the same result  
   217→    // (every team without a type gets 'open'), so the last write wins safely.  
   218→    // The migrationDone flag ensures we only persist the migration once per process.  
   219→    let needsSave = false  
   220→    for (const team of teams) {  
   221→      if (!team.type) {  
   222→        team.type = 'open'  
   223→        needsSave = true  
   224→      }  
   225→    }  
   226→    // CC-003: Migration write is idempotent and safe without lock — worst case is a redundant write.  
   227→    // When called from getTeam() (no lock), two concurrent migrations may both write, but produce identical output.  
   228→    if (needsSave && !migrationDone) {  
   229→      migrationDone = true  
   230→      saveTeams(teams)  
   231→    }  
   232→  
   233→    return teams  
   234→  } catch (error) {  
   235→    console.error('Failed to load teams:', error)  
   236→    return []  
   237→  }  
   238→}

   247→    console.error('Failed to save teams:', error)  
   248→    return false

     1→/**  
     2→ * Document Registry - File-based CRUD for team document persistence  
     3→ *  
     4→ * Storage: ~/.aimaestro/teams/docs-{teamId}.json (one per team)  
     5→ * Mirrors the pattern from lib/task-registry.ts  
     6→ */  
     7→  
     8→import fs from 'fs'  
     9→import path from 'path'  
    10→import os from 'os'  
    11→import { v4 as uuidv4 } from 'uuid'  
    12→import { withLock } from '@/lib/file-lock'  
    13→import type { TeamDocument, TeamDocumentsFile } from '@/types/document'  
    14→  
    15→const TEAMS_DIR = path.join(os.homedir(), '.aimaestro', 'teams')  
    16→  
    17→function ensureTeamsDir() {  
    18→  if (!fs.existsSync(TEAMS_DIR)) {  
    19→    fs.mkdirSync(TEAMS_DIR, { recursive: true })  
    20→  }  
    21→}  
    22→  
    23→function docsFilePath(teamId: string): string {  
    24→  // Validate teamId is a strict UUID to prevent path traversal (CC-001)  
    25→  if (!/^[0-9a-f]{8}-[0-9a-f]{4}-[0-9a-f]{4}-[0-9a-f]{4}-[0-9a-f]{12}$/i.test(teamId))  
    26→    throw new Error('Invalid team ID')  
    27→  // path.basename() as defense-in-depth against directory traversal  
    28→  return path.join(TEAMS_DIR, path.basename(`docs-${teamId}.json`))  
    29→}  
    30→  
    31→export function loadDocuments(teamId: string): TeamDocument[] {  
    32→  try {  
    33→    ensureTeamsDir()  
    34→    const filePath = docsFilePath(teamId)  
    35→    if (!fs.existsSync(filePath)) {  
    36→      return []  
    37→    }  
    38→    const data = fs.readFileSync(filePath, 'utf-8')  
    39→    const parsed: TeamDocumentsFile = JSON.parse(data)

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-20 12:42:12]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

I found it. The `createTeam` function at line 278 uses `data.type ?? 'open'` but does NOT apply `result.sanitized.type`. If `validateTeamMutation` decides to auto-downgrade a closed team to open (line 131 of team-registry: `sanitized.type = 'open'`), that auto-downgrade is IGNORED in createTeam. This is a logic bug in team-registry, not in teams-service, but teams-service relies on this behavior.  

Now let me check whether there is also a similar issue in updateTeam where the `sanitized` is applied properly.  

I can see at line 333-338 of team-registry.ts, updateTeam does `const finalUpdates = { ...updates, ...result.sanitized }` which correctly applies the sanitized type override. But createTeam at line 272-282 does NOT use the sanitized fields for `type` and `chiefOfStaffId` -- it only uses sanitized for `name` and `agentIds`.  

Now let me also check the `[id]/documents/[docId]/route.ts` for the missing requestingAgentId.  

Looking at the route files more carefully:  

**`[id]/documents/[docId]/route.ts` lines 6, 10, 30, 39-43:**  
- GET: `_request` (unused), calls `getTeamDocument(id, docId)` with only 2 args -- but the service function signature is `getTeamDocument(teamId, docId, requestingAgentId?)` (3 params). No requestingAgentId passed. This is functional but ACL is bypassed.  
- PUT: No `requestingAgentId` extracted or passed to `updateTeamDocument`. Body is passed directly without stripping `requestingAgentId`.   
- DELETE: No `requestingAgentId` extracted or passed to `deleteTeamDocument`.  

Now I have all findings. Let me write the report.  

</div>

     2→    
     3→ - One agent must get the title of MANAGER. Only one agent can be MANAGER at any time.

     5→ - The MANAGER is the only agent that can send/receive messages to/from every other agent (no restrictions).

Any agent is eligible unless it is already a chief-of-staff in another team.

   204→  
   205→export function loadTeams(): Team[] {  
   206→  try {  
   207→    ensureTeamsDir()  
   208→    if (!fs.existsSync(TEAMS_FILE)) {  
   209→      return []  
   210→    }  
   211→    const data = fs.readFileSync(TEAMS_FILE, 'utf-8')  
   212→    const parsed: TeamsFile = JSON.parse(data)  
   213→    const teams = Array.isArray(parsed.teams) ? parsed.teams : []  
   214→  
   215→    // Idempotent convergent migration: ensure all teams have a type field (default to 'open').  
   216→    // If two concurrent calls both trigger the migration, both produce the same result  
   217→    // (every team without a type gets 'open'), so the last write wins safely.  
   218→    // The migrationDone flag ensures we only persist the migration once per process.  
   219→    let needsSave = false  
   220→    for (const team of teams) {  
   221→      if (!team.type) {  
   222→        team.type = 'open'  
   223→        needsSave = true  
   224→      }  
   225→    }  
   226→    // CC-003: Migration write is idempotent and safe without lock — worst case is a redundant write.  
   227→    // When called from getTeam() (no lock), two concurrent migrations may both write, but produce identical output.  
   228→    if (needsSave && !migrationDone) {  
   229→      migrationDone = true  
   230→      saveTeams(teams)  
   231→    }  
   232→  
   233→    return teams  
   234→  } catch (error) {  
   235→    console.error('Failed to load teams:', error)  
   236→    return []  
   237→  }  
   238→}  
   239→  
   240→export function saveTeams(teams: Team[]): boolean {  
   241→  try {  
   242→    ensureTeamsDir()  
   243→    const file: TeamsFile = { version: 1, teams }  
   244→    fs.writeFileSync(TEAMS_FILE, JSON.stringify(file, null, 2), 'utf-8')  
   245→    return true  
   246→  } catch (error) {  
   247→    console.error('Failed to save teams:', error)  
   248→    return false  
   249→  }  
   250→}

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-20 12:41:52]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Good -- `updateTeam` correctly applies `result.sanitized` at line 333 (`const finalUpdates = { ...updates, ...result.sanitized }`), so G5 works for updates. But `createTeam` does NOT apply `result.sanitized.type`. Let me verify this is truly a bug by checking: can `createTeam` ever trigger the G5 path? The G5 path triggers when `effectiveType === 'closed' && !effectiveCOS`. In `createTeam`, this would happen if someone creates a team with `type: 'closed'` but no `chiefOfStaffId`. Let me verify this scenario.  

Looking at line 130-131 of `validateTeamMutation`:  
```
if (effectiveType === 'closed' && !effectiveCOS) {
    sanitized.type = 'open'
}
```

And line 134-136:  
```
if (effectiveType === 'open' && effectiveCOS) {
    return { valid: false, ... }
}
```

Note that after line 131 sets `sanitized.type = 'open'`, the check at line 134 uses `effectiveType` which is still `'closed'` (the local variable wasn't updated). So the COS-on-open check at line 134 won't trigger a false rejection. That's fine -- it means validation will PASS with `sanitized.type = 'open'`, but `createTeam` at line 278 uses `data.type ?? 'open'` which is `'closed'` (the original data), ignoring the sanitized downgrade.  

This IS a real bug: G5 auto-downgrade doesn't work in `createTeam`.

This error message is now inaccurate -- it doesn't mention that COS can also message agents not in any closed team (the G1 fix at lines 114-118). According to v2 Rule 21, COS can belong to unlimited open teams. This seems wrong.

I also notice a more subtle issue: The G5 auto-downgrade at lines 130-131 sets `sanitized.type = 'open'`, but the subsequent multi-closed-team check at line 167 uses `effectiveType` (still `'closed'`), not the sanitized type. Wait, let me re-think this. If `effectiveType === 'closed'` and `!effectiveCOS`, the G5 downgrade fires and sets `sanitized.type = 'open'`. This means agents could be wrongly rejected from joining a team that's being auto-downgraded to open.  

However, this scenario is somewhat edge-case-y: creating a "closed" team with no COS. The UI should prevent this, and the main path is that a closed team losing its COS gets downgraded via updateTeam (which correctly applies sanitized). So I'll categorize this as SHOULD-FIX, not MUST-FIX.

- An open-team agent sending to COS: sender is NOT in closed team, recipient IS in closed team (COS is in a closed team's agentIds). This hits Step 6 at line 148: "Cannot message agents in closed teams from outside". So an open-team agent CANNOT message a COS.

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-20 12:42:23]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Confirmed: `TeamValidationException` is imported but never used. In the original API route, there's a `catch (error) { if (error instanceof TeamValidationException) { ... } }` block that handles it. The service has NO try/catch around the main logic of `resolveTransferReq`, meaning if `loadTeams()` or `saveTeams()` throws a `TeamValidationException`, it will propagate unhandled.  

Now let me check the `setGovernancePassword` ordering issue -- the service sets password BEFORE logging:  

Looking at the service file (lines 141-147): `await setPassword(password)` is called, THEN `const isChange = !!config.passwordHash`. But `config` was loaded at line 121 BEFORE calling `setPassword`, so `config.passwordHash` still reflects the old value. This is actually fine -- it correctly detects whether it was a change or a new set. However, the API route (lines 45-52) does: `const isChange = !!config.passwordHash` BEFORE `setPassword` -- so the order differs but both are logically correct since `config` is the snapshot.  

Wait, actually in the service file the order is:  
1. `await setPassword(password)` (line 141)  
2. `const isChange = !!config.passwordHash` (line 142)  

While in the API route:  
1. `const isChange = !!config.passwordHash` (line 45)  
2. `await setPassword(password)` (line 46)  

Both work because `config` is a snapshot from line 121/20 respectively. But the service order is slightly misleading (reads `config.passwordHash` after `setPassword` returns, which could confuse readers). This is a NIT, not a bug.

     2→ * Simple in-memory rate limiter for governance password operations.

    13→// Phase 2: use atomic increment.  
    14→  
    15→/** Check if the rate limit allows another attempt */  
    16→export function checkRateLimit(  
    17→  key: string,  
    18→  maxAttempts: number = DEFAULT_MAX_ATTEMPTS,  
    19→  windowMs: number = DEFAULT_WINDOW_MS  
    20→): { allowed: boolean; retryAfterMs: number } {

    22→  const entry = limits.get(key)  
    23→  
    24→  // Window expired — reset  
    25→  if (entry && now >= entry.resetAt) {  
    26→    limits.delete(key)  
    27→    return { allowed: true, retryAfterMs: 0 }  
    28→  }  
    29→  
    30→  // Check if over limit

    32→    return { allowed: false, retryAfterMs: entry.resetAt - now }  
    33→  }  
    34→  
    35→  return { allowed: true, retryAfterMs: 0 }

    40→  let entry = limits.get(key)  
    41→  const now = Date.now()  
    42→  // Reset expired windows so stale counts are not reused  
    43→  if (entry && now >= entry.resetAt) { entry = undefined; limits.delete(key) }

    45→  limits.set(key, { count: fresh.count + 1, resetAt: fresh.resetAt })

   200→  
   201→// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------  
   202→// GET /api/governance/transfers?teamId=...&agentId=...&status=...  
   203→// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------  
   204→export function listTransferRequests(query: {  
   205→  teamId?: string | null  
   206→  agentId?: string | null  
   207→  status?: string | null  
   208→}): ServiceResult<{ requests: any[] }> {  
   209→  const { teamId, agentId, status } = query  
   210→  
   211→  if (status && !['pending', 'approved', 'rejected'].includes(status)) {  
   212→    return { error: 'Invalid status filter', status: 400 }  
   213→  }  
   214→  
   215→  let requests = loadTransfers()  
   216→  
   217→  if (teamId) {  
   218→    requests = requests.filter(r => r.fromTeamId === teamId || r.toTeamId === teamId)  
   219→  }  
   220→  if (agentId) {  
   221→    requests = requests.filter(r => r.agentId === agentId)  
   222→  }  
   223→  if (status) {  
   224→    requests = requests.filter(r => r.status === status)  
   225→  }  
   226→  
   227→  return { data: { requests }, status: 200 }  
   228→}

   317→function sendServiceResult(res: ServerResponse, result: any) {  
   318→  if (result.error && !result.data) {  
   319→    sendJson(res, result.status || 500, { error: result.error }, result.headers)  
   320→  } else {  
   321→    sendJson(res, result.status || 200, result.data, result.headers)  
   322→  }  
   323→}  

</details>


## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-20 12:42:00]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

This confirms the bug. `sendServiceResult` takes `result: any` -- if you pass a Promise, then `result.error` is `undefined` and `result.data` is `undefined`, so it goes to the else branch and sends `sendJson(res, 200, undefined)`. This is a real bug -- the async service results won't be awaited.  

Let me now check a few more things: the `updateTeamById` and `deleteTeamById` and `createNewTeam` also need checking.  

From the grep results:  
- `updateTeamById` is `async` (line 198) -- in router at line 1192: `sendServiceResult(res, updateTeamById(...))` -- NO `await` -- **BUG**  
- `deleteTeamById` is `async` (line 233) -- in router at line 1196: `sendServiceResult(res, deleteTeamById(...))` -- NO `await` -- **BUG**  
- `createNewTeam` is `async` (line 131) -- in router at line 1204: `sendServiceResult(res, createNewTeam(...))` -- NO `await` -- **BUG**  

Now let me check the `getTeamDocument` and `deleteTeamDocument` calls. `getTeamDocument` is sync (line 499), `deleteTeamDocument` is async (line 568). In the router: `deleteTeamDocument(params.id, params.docId)` at line 1174 -- NO `await` -- **BUG**. Also note this call is missing `requestingAgentId` parameter.  

Let me also check `updateTeamDocument`:  
- `updateTeamDocument` is `async` (line 525) -- in router at line 1171: NO `await` -- **BUG**  

And `createTeamDocument`:  
- `createTeamDocument` is `async` (line 459) -- in router at line 1183: NO `await` -- **BUG**  

Now let me also check the `updateTeamDocument` and `deleteTeamDocument` signatures to see if `requestingAgentId` is needed.  

</div>

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-20 12:42:13]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Now I need to check if `deleteTeamDocument` in the router is missing `requestingAgentId`. Let me re-read line 1173.  

Looking at line 1173-1174:  
```typescript
{ method: 'DELETE', pattern: /^\/api\/teams\/([^/]+)\/documents\/([^/]+)$/, paramNames: ['id', 'docId'], handler: async (_req, res, params) => {
    sendServiceResult(res, deleteTeamDocument(params.id, params.docId))
```

The `deleteTeamDocument` function accepts `requestingAgentId?: string` as a third parameter, and the router does NOT extract X-Agent-Id for this route. This means governance ACL checks won't be enforced for document deletion. That's a security issue.  

Also, let me check `updateTeamDocument` (line 1169-1171):  
```typescript
{ method: 'PUT', pattern: /^\/api\/teams\/([^/]+)\/documents\/([^/]+)$/, paramNames: ['id', 'docId'], handler: async (req, res, params) => {
    const body = await readJsonBody(req)
    sendServiceResult(res, updateTeamDocument(params.id, params.docId, body))
```

The `updateTeamDocument` expects `requestingAgentId` inside `params` (as part of `UpdateDocumentParams`). The body should already contain it if the client sends it. But unlike other routes, the router is NOT extracting X-Agent-Id header and adding it to the body. Let me check how other document routes handle it...  

Looking at `createTeamDocument` (line 1180-1183):  
```typescript
const requestingAgentId = getHeader(req, 'X-Agent-Id') || undefined
sendServiceResult(res, createTeamDocument(params.id, { ...body, requestingAgentId }))
```

So `createTeamDocument` DOES extract X-Agent-Id and pass it in. But `updateTeamDocument` at line 1171 does NOT. And `deleteTeamDocument` at line 1174 does NOT either. This is inconsistent and means governance ACL won't work for document updates and deletes.  

Similarly, `getTeamDocument` at line 1167 does NOT extract X-Agent-Id, but the function signature accepts `requestingAgentId?: string` as the third parameter:  

```typescript
export function getTeamDocument(teamId: string, docId: string, requestingAgentId?: string): ServiceResult<{ document: any }>
```

Let me now write the report.

   202→export function extractApiKeyFromHeader(authHeader: string | null): string | null {  
   203→  if (!authHeader) return null  
   204→  
   205→  if (authHeader.startsWith('Bearer ')) {  
   206→    return authHeader.substring(7)  
   207→  }  
   208→

   210→  if (isValidApiKeyFormat(authHeader)) {  
   211→    return authHeader  
   212→  }  
   213→  
   214→  return null  
   215→}  
   216→  
   217→/**  
   218→ * Rotate an API key  
   219→ * Creates a new key and sets expiration on the old one  
   220→ */  
   221→export function rotateApiKey(oldApiKey: string): AMPKeyRotationResponse | null {  
   222→  const keys = loadApiKeys()  
   223→  const oldKeyHash = hashApiKey(oldApiKey)  
   224→  
   225→  const oldRecord = keys.find(k => k.key_hash === oldKeyHash && k.status === 'active')  
   226→  if (!oldRecord) {  
   227→    return null  
   228→  }  
   229→  
   230→  // Create new key  
   231→  const newApiKey = generateApiKey()  
   232→  const newKeyHash = hashApiKey(newApiKey)  
   233→  
   234→  const now = new Date()  
   235→  const graceExpiry = new Date(now.getTime() + KEY_ROTATION_GRACE_PERIOD_MS)  
   236→  
   237→  // Update old key with expiration  
   238→  oldRecord.expires_at = graceExpiry.toISOString()  
   239→  
   240→  // Create new key record  
   241→  const newRecord: AMPApiKeyRecord = {  
   242→    key_hash: newKeyHash,  
   243→    agent_id: oldRecord.agent_id,  
   244→    tenant_id: oldRecord.tenant_id,  
   245→    address: oldRecord.address,  
   246→    created_at: now.toISOString(),  
   247→    expires_at: null,  
   248→    status: 'active'  
   249→  }  
   250→  
   251→  keys.push(newRecord)  
   252→  saveApiKeys(keys)  
   253→  
   254→  console.log(`[AMP Auth] Rotated API key for agent ${oldRecord.agent_id.substring(0, 8)}...`)  
   255→  
   256→  return {  
   257→    api_key: newApiKey,  
   258→    expires_at: null,  
   259→    previous_key_valid_until: graceExpiry.toISOString()  
   260→  }  
   261→}

     1→/**  
     2→ * Team Resource ACL — checks whether an agent (or web UI request)  
     3→ * is allowed to access a given team's resources.  
     4→ *  
     5→ * Open teams (type undefined or 'open') impose no restrictions.

    23→/**  
    24→ * Determine whether the requester may access the team's resources.  
    25→ *  
    26→ * Decision order:  
    27→ *  1. Web UI (no agentId)      → allowed  
    28→ *  2. Team not found           → denied (caller handles 404)  
    29→ *  3. Team is open / untyped   → allowed  
    30→ *  4. Requester is MANAGER     → allowed  
    31→ *  5. Requester is chief-of-staff → allowed  
    32→ *  6. Requester is a member    → allowed  
    33→ *  7. Otherwise                → denied  
    34→ */

    39→  // where all local processes are trusted.

    41→  // genuine web UI requests from other local processes.  
    42→  if (input.requestingAgentId === undefined) {  
    43→    return { allowed: true }  
    44→  }

   420→  }

   423→/**  
   424→ * Verify a message signature with the sender's public key  
   425→ */  
   426→export function verifySignature(  
   427→  message: string,  
   428→  signature: string,  
   429→  publicKeyHex: string  
   430→): boolean {  
   431→  try {  
   432→    const { verify, createPublicKey } = require('crypto')  
   433→  
   434→    // Reconstruct public key from hex  
   435→    // Ed25519 SPKI header (12 bytes) + public key (32 bytes)  
   436→    const header = Buffer.from([  
   437→      0x30, 0x2a, 0x30, 0x05, 0x06, 0x03, 0x2b, 0x65, 0x70, 0x03, 0x21, 0x00  
   438→    ])  
   439→    const publicKeyBytes = Buffer.from(publicKeyHex, 'hex')  
   440→    const spkiDer = Buffer.concat([header, publicKeyBytes])  
   441→  
   442→    const publicKey = createPublicKey({  
   443→      key: spkiDer,  
   444→      format: 'der',  
   445→      type: 'spki'  
   446→    })  
   447→  
   448→    const signatureBuffer = Buffer.from(signature, 'base64')  
   449→    return verify(null, Buffer.from(message), publicKey, signatureBuffer)  
   450→  } catch (error) {  
   451→    const errMsg = error instanceof Error ? error.message : String(error)  
   452→    console.warn(`[AMP Keys] Signature verification failed: ${errMsg} (publicKeyHex length: ${publicKeyHex?.length || 0})`)  
   453→    return false  
   454→  }  
   455→}  

</details>

    29→    if (agentId) {  
    30→      requests = requests.filter(r => r.agentId === agentId)  
    31→    }  
    32→    if (status) {  
    33→      requests = requests.filter(r => r.status === status)  
    34→    }  
    35→  
    36→    return NextResponse.json({ requests })  
    37→  } catch (error) {  
    38→    console.error('Error loading transfers:', error)  
    39→    return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Internal server error' }, { status: 500 })  
    40→  }  
    41→}

     1	/**  
     2	 * Message Filter — enforces closed-team messaging isolation  
     3	 *  
     4	 * Determines whether a message from sender to recipient is allowed  
     5	 * based on governance roles (MANAGER, Chief-of-Staff) and closed-team  
     6	 * membership. Open-world agents (not in any closed team) can message  
     7	 * freely unless the recipient is inside a closed team.  
     8	 */  
     9

    11	import { loadTeams } from './team-registry'  
    12	import { isValidUuid } from './validation'

    14	export interface MessageFilterInput {  
    15	  senderAgentId: string | null // null = mesh-forwarded message  
    16	  recipientAgentId: string  
    17	}  
    18	  
    19	export interface MessageFilterResult {  
    20	  allowed: boolean  
    21	  reason?: string  
    22	}  
    23	  
    24	/**  
    25	 * Check whether a message from sender to recipient is allowed.  
    26	 *  
    27	 * Algorithm (R6.1–R6.7):  
    28	 * 1. Mesh-forwarded (senderAgentId null): denied if recipient is in a closed team (unverified sender)  
    29	 * 1b. Unresolved recipient (alias, not UUID) from closed-team sender: denied (prevents bypass)  
    30	 * 2. Neither in a closed team: allowed (open world, current behavior) (R6.4)  
    31	 * 3. Sender is MANAGER: always allowed (R6.3)  
    32	 * 4. Sender is COS of any closed team: can reach MANAGER, other COS, own team members (R6.2)  
    33	 * 5. Normal closed-team member: can reach same-team members and own COS (R6.1)  
    34	 * 6. Outside sender to closed-team recipient: denied (R6.5) — always reached after Steps 2–5  
    35	 *  
    36	 * IMPORTANT (R6.7): Uses getClosedTeamsForAgent (plural) to correctly handle  
    37	 * COS agents who belong to multiple closed teams simultaneously.  
    38	 */

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-20 05:33:51]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Now I see the issue with the message-filter test. The test at line 182 says "denies COS messaging an agent outside all their teams" and expects the reason to contain "own team members". But the code at line 122 says "Chief-of-Staff can only message MANAGER, other Chiefs-of-Staff, and own team members". However, with the G1 rule added (line 116), a COS can now message agents NOT in any closed team. The OUTSIDER is not in any closed team, so this would be allowed now with G1.

    13→    readFileSync: vi.fn((filePath: string) => {  
    14→      if (filePath in fsStore) return fsStore[filePath]  
    15→      throw new Error(`ENOENT: no such file or directory, open '${filePath}'`)  
    16→    }),  
    17→    writeFileSync: vi.fn((filePath: string, data: string) => {  
    18→      fsStore[filePath] = data  
    19→    }),  
    20→  },  
    21→}))  
    22→  
    23→let uuidCounter = 0

    26→    uuidCounter++

    28→    const hex = uuidCounter.toString(16).padStart(12, '0')  
    29→    return `00000000-0000-4000-a000-${hex}`  
    30→  }),  
    31→}))

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-20 05:34:24]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Now I have a comprehensive understanding of all the issues. Let me summarize:  

**Issue 1: Routes not awaiting async service functions**  
- `app/api/teams/route.ts` line 23: `createNewTeam` is async but not awaited  
- `app/api/teams/[id]/route.ts` line 34: `updateTeamById` is async but not awaited    
- `app/api/teams/[id]/route.ts` line 49: `deleteTeamById` is async but not awaited  
- `app/api/teams/[id]/documents/route.ts` line 34: `createTeamDocument` is async but not awaited  
- `app/api/teams/[id]/documents/[docId]/route.ts` line 30: `updateTeamDocument` is async but not awaited  
- `app/api/teams/[id]/documents/[docId]/route.ts` line 44: `deleteTeamDocument` is async but not awaited  

**Issue 2: teams-service.test.ts mock doesn't include TeamValidationException**  
The mock for `@/lib/team-registry` doesn't include `TeamValidationException`, plus additional mocks needed for governance, team-acl, validation, agent-registry.  

**Issue 3: teams-service.test.ts - functions are now async but tests call them sync**  
Many functions changed from sync to async (createNewTeam, updateTeamById, deleteTeamById, etc.)  

**Issue 4: document-api.test.ts missing mocks for governance, team-acl, validation, agent-registry**  

**Issue 5: team-api.test.ts - route calls not awaited for async service functions**  

**Issue 6: message-filter.test.ts - G1 rule changes expected behavior for COS messaging outsiders**  
The test "denies COS messaging an agent outside all their teams" expects denial but G1 now allows COS to message open-world agents.  

**Issue 7: validate-team-mutation.test.ts - G5 rule changed closed-team-without-COS behavior**  
The test expects rejection but G5 now auto-downgrades to open instead.  

**Issue 8: message-filter.ts missing mock for validation module**  

Let me fix all these issues systematically. Let me start with the route files that need `await`.  

</div>

    updateTeamDocument('team-1', 'doc-1', { title: 'New Title' })

    expect(mockDocs.updateDocument).toHaveBeenCalledWith('team-1', 'doc-1', { title: 'New Title' })
  })

  it('passes pinned and tags when provided', () => {
    mockDocs.updateDocument.mockReturnValue(makeDocument())

    updateTeamDocument('team-1', 'doc-1', { pinned: true, tags: ['api'] })

    expect(mockDocs.updateDocument).toHaveBeenCalledWith('team-1', 'doc-1', { pinned: true, tags: ['api'] })
  })

  it('returns 404 when document not found', () => {
    mockDocs.updateDocument.mockReturnValue(null)

    const result = updateTeamDocument('team-1', 'nope', { title: 'X' })

    expect(result.status).toBe(404)
  })

  it('returns 500 when updateDocument throws', () => {
    mockDocs.updateDocument.mockImplementation(() => { throw new Error('write error') })

    const result = updateTeamDocument('team-1', 'doc-1', { title: 'X' })

    expect(result.status).toBe(500)
  })
})
```

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-20 05:38:37]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Looking at the G2 rule more carefully and the code in team-registry.ts, the multi-closed-team constraint says "COS is NOT exempt from multi-closed-team constraint (v2 Rule 21: max 1 closed team)". Let me re-read the code at lines 163-187.  

The code says at line 165: "COS is NOT exempt from multi-closed-team constraint (v2 Rule 21: max 1 closed team)". However, at line 173 it only skips MANAGER, not COS. And at line 170, it says "Skip agents already in the existing team (not newly added)". So the COS being in an existing closed team WOULD now be rejected since the COS exemption was removed.  

Wait, let me look more carefully at the test at line 334. It has `cosAgentId = 'agent-promoted-cos'` already in `team-existing`. The new mutation creates a NEW team with `cosAgentId` as COS. Since `cosAgentId` is already in `team-existing` (a closed team), and the new team is also closed, the constraint should reject it under G2.  

But wait -- looking at line 170: "Skip agents already in the existing team (not newly added)". This check is `if (existingTeam?.agentIds.includes(agentId)) continue`. For a CREATE operation, `existingTeam` is null (since `teamId` is null for create), so the check doesn't skip anyone. So `cosAgentId` would be checked against `teams`, and since it's in `team-existing` which is closed, it WOULD be rejected.  

This means these two tests (lines 334 and 363) need to be updated to expect rejection under G2.  

</div>

   121→export function listAllTeams(): ServiceResult<{ teams: any[] }> {  
   122→  const teams = loadTeams()

   124→}  
   125→  
   126→/**  
   127→ * Create a new team.  
   128→ * Governance: validates team type, passes managerId and agentNames to createTeam  
   129→ * for business rule enforcement (R1-R4).  
   130→ */  
   131→export async function createNewTeam(params: CreateTeamParams): Promise<ServiceResult<{ team: any }>> {  
   132→  const { name, description, agentIds } = params  
   133→  
   134→  if (!name || typeof name !== 'string') {  
   135→    return { error: 'Team name is required', status: 400 }  
   136→  }  
   137→  
   138→  if (agentIds && !Array.isArray(agentIds)) {  
   139→    return { error: 'agentIds must be an array', status: 400 }  
   140→  }  
   141→  
   142→  // Governance: validate type field  
   143→  if (params.type && params.type !== 'open' && params.type !== 'closed') {  
   144→    return { error: 'type must be "open" or "closed"', status: 400 }  
   145→  }  
   146→  
   147→  try {  
   148→    // Pass governance context (managerId + agent names for collision checks) to createTeam  
   149→    const managerId = getManagerId()  
   150→    const agentNames = loadAgents().map(a => a.name).filter(Boolean)  
   151→    const team = await createTeam(  
   152→      { name, description, agentIds: agentIds || [], type: params.type, chiefOfStaffId: params.chiefOfStaffId },  
   153→      managerId,  
   154→      agentNames  
   155→    )  
   156→    return { data: { team }, status: 201 }  
   157→  } catch (error) {  
   158→    // TeamValidationException carries a specific HTTP status code from governance rules  
   159→    if (error instanceof TeamValidationException) {  
   160→      return { error: error.message, status: error.code }  
   161→    }  
   162→    console.error('Failed to create team:', error)  
   163→    return { error: error instanceof Error ? error.message : 'Failed to create team', status: 500 }  
   164→  }  
   165→}

I need to update the test expectation.

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Down to 1 failure. The document-api test expects "Team not found" for a PUT to a non-existent team, but the actual error is "Document not found". Looking at the `updateTeamDocument` function in the service -- it does NOT check team existence first, it goes straight to `updateDocument`. But the test CC-005 expects it to check team existence first.  

Looking at the service code:  

```typescript
export async function updateTeamDocument(
  teamId: string,
  docId: string,
  params: UpdateDocumentParams
): Promise<ServiceResult<{ document: any }>> {
  // Governance ACL: closed teams restrict mutations to manager, COS, and members
  const { requestingAgentId, ...docFields } = params
  if (requestingAgentId) {
    const access = checkTeamAccess({ teamId, requestingAgentId })
    ...
  }

  try {
    const updates: Record<string, unknown> = {}
    ...
    const document = await updateDocument(teamId, docId, updates as any)
    if (!document) {
      return { error: 'Document not found', status: 404 }
    }
```

The service doesn't check `getTeam(teamId)` first. The test expects "Team not found" for a missing team. I need to add a team existence check to `updateTeamDocument`.  

</div>


## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-20 05:41:44]*

export async function updateTeamDocument(
  teamId: string,
  docId: string,

```

**New:**  
```
export async function updateTeamDocument(
  teamId: string,
  docId: string,
  params: UpdateDocumentParams
): Promise<ServiceResult<{ document: any }>> {
  // Validate team exists before attempting document update (CC-005)
  const team = getTeam(teamId)
  if (!team) {
    return { error: 'Team not found', status: 404 }
  }

  // Governance ACL: closed teams restrict mutations to manager, COS, and members
  const { requestingAgentId, ...docFields } = params
```
